  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fe06e17c-b4b7-4c55-8159-cdfc174d5df8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1941405285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1941405285" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1941405285?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941405285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer497597128343227020"><b>A buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maria</a>.</b><br/><br/>In the last novella (chronologically) the Dendarii mercenary fleet took some serious beating and manage to get a mighty Empire seriously pissed off. The result: there was a really nice juicy reward for Miles Vorkosigan aka Admiral Naismith and the fleet had to escape into a remote peaceful place for much-needed repairs. <br/><br/>From the moment I began reading the series I wondered what happened to good old mother Earth.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426405177i/14012467._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='Earth' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Here my question was finally answered as the remote</span>
  <span id="freeText497597128343227020" style="display:none"><b>A buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a>.</b><br><br>In the last novella (chronologically) the Dendarii mercenary fleet took some serious beating and manage to get a mighty Empire seriously pissed off. The result: there was a really nice juicy reward for Miles Vorkosigan aka Admiral Naismith and the fleet had to escape into a remote peaceful place for much-needed repairs. <br><br>From the moment I began reading the series I wondered what happened to good old mother Earth.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426405177i/14012467._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="Earth" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Here my question was finally answered as the remote peaceful place happened to be our own planet - its future version that is. Miles being Miles, he stumbled right in the middle of conspiracy involving his own Empire; a long way from it I might add. Once again because this is Miles we are talking about this happened to be his least significant problem. His payment for the last job disappeared somewhere and he had no money to pay for the repairs and medical treatment of his injured crew. <br><br>He also had to keep himself and his alter ego Admiral Naismith as two separate people; it would take pages and paged if I try to explain the complications resulting in people realizing these two are the same person. So he had what he thought a brilliant idea and explained that Admiral Naismith is his illegal clone. This brought even more severe (and almost lethal) unexpected complications to Miles' life.<br><br>My personal opinion is that this is one of the weakest books of the series so far. I almost gave the book 3 stars, but some events in the very end made me raise the rating and believe me: I grumbled a lot doing it. It seems my low opinion is echoed by at least one of my buddy readers as Maria mentioned 3 stars as well.<br><br>You might have guessed the good parts: interesting plot, great characters, and equally great locations (hey, I think our planet is severely underrated in a lot of space opera books). My job here is to talk about weak parts. Miles brooded too much for my tastes and these parts brought aforementioned exciting plot to a screeching halt. <br><br>There was one cliche of literature used which was old at the time they began writing The Epic of Gilgamesh. We all know and really hate this one: a good guy captures a bad guy after lots and lots of troubles, looks at him, takes a pity and lets the baddy go only to get stabbed in the back by him a couple of pages later. One example of such would be Elric of Melniboné; I am sure any reader can come up with his own. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490489322i/22318762._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="320" alt="Elric" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The set up of this book gives me an idea I can predict exactly what would happen in the next one and somehow it lowers my enthusiasm about that read. I hope I am wrong though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="497597128343227020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874231180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874231180" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874231180?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=advanture">advanture</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874231180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11414085375991333573"><b>*** 4 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria because we need some FORWARD MOMENTUM!!!</b><br/><br/>Gosh, what can I say about this Universe where Miles Vorkosigan rains supreme? IT IS AWESOME!!! <br/><br/>Yes, yes, as I said in my review of the previous book, I passed from the level of an objective reader to the zone of fan-girl subjectivity. I am a fan. So, take my review in the spirit in which it is intended, which is just to gush over my love for the genius of Louis McMaster Bujold and her unfailing ability to write </span>
  <span id="freeText11414085375991333573" style="display:none"><b>*** 4 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria because we need some FORWARD MOMENTUM!!!</b><br /><br />Gosh, what can I say about this Universe where Miles Vorkosigan rains supreme? IT IS AWESOME!!! <br /><br />Yes, yes, as I said in my review of the previous book, I passed from the level of an objective reader to the zone of fan-girl subjectivity. I am a fan. So, take my review in the spirit in which it is intended, which is just to gush over my love for the genius of Louis McMaster Bujold and her unfailing ability to write a story full of action and intrigues, but most of all a story full of heart and charm oozing of the pages.. It has gotten to the point where if I had to choose a literary world I would like to spend time in order to feel good and emerge with some positivity from, this is the world I would choose any time! And I am not sure what makes me feel this way, because there are plenty of bad things happening and vileins running around causing trouble.. <br /><br />This book Miles, Quinn and Ivan all end up on old Earth at the same time. The Naismith mercenaries need a break, the heavily wounded need medical care, the ships need repair and supplies, and Miles has to get the money to do it all. Supposedly the Barrayaran Empire's ambassador should have a check for them, but that would have been to easy and Miles gets stuck at the Embassy indefinitely. It would have been OK if he didn't have to keep on playing the role of Admiral Naismith and lieutenant Vorkosigan at the same time, trying to keep his cover and not give out the information that they are really working for Barrayar. So he comes up with a story that Naismith is a clone of Vorkosigan gone rogue seven years ago... Now if only the story could stick....<br /><br />Of course things got complicated, of course everyone tried to kill him and the suspects were numerous. Nothing ever is easy for the little dude. He even had some semi-successful attempt at getting himself laid, but that has not been a true problem as of late, has it?:-)<br /><br />The story introduced a new character who I am sure we will hear from again - to good for soap opera like machinations for the author not to use it again, despite many feeling like it is a cop out plot device. I don't mind as long as we get more of our Miles and the crew!!!<br /><br />Once again, the moral dilemma of the hour is cloning and the effects it has on both the clone and the one cloned. What would you do if you were faced with the existence of a second you, as close to a copy as it could possibly get. Do you want to get to know them, bring them into the family, use them for parts? And as always, the author handled it graciously and with no judgement. I love this author!!!<br /><br />Now, to all the fans of lighter Sci-fi and adventure, I whole heatedly recommend this series!!! Try it out, I think you might be pleasantly surprised:-)<br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you need in the pages of a Good book!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11414085375991333573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_778437775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/778437775" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/778437775?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781886778740" href="/book/show/6239196-brothers-in-arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=scifi-60s-70s-80s">scifi-60s-70s-80s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=x-vorkosigan-saga">x-vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer778437775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2813423775773645109">so how tall is Tyrion the Imp anyway? I think Miles Vorkosigan is well under 5 foot. both characters are brilliant, idiosyncratic, lovelorn, and really full of themselves. I always thought that Tyrion was a complete original but there's a lot of Miles in him and Miles came first, right? I suppose it doesn't matter who came first, what matters to me is that these are two of my favorite creations in all of genre fiction. well I've always had a fondness for short guys with big brains. Miles actuall</span>
  <span id="freeText2813423775773645109" style="display:none">so how tall is Tyrion the Imp anyway? I think Miles Vorkosigan is well under 5 foot. both characters are brilliant, idiosyncratic, lovelorn, and really full of themselves. I always thought that Tyrion was a complete original but there's a lot of Miles in him and Miles came first, right? I suppose it doesn't matter who came first, what matters to me is that these are two of my favorite creations in all of genre fiction. well I've always had a fondness for short guys with big brains. Miles actually calls himself a genius again, second time I've seen this. oh, Miles. Bujold you are awesome for making sure your wonderful creation has his own flaws that are completely separate from his physical flaws, that crooked spine, those brittle bones, those little legs, poor adorable Miles. well at least he finally gets laid. Bujold you are also awesome for spinning another fun yarn that moves fast and still manages to think deep at times too, dropping things like <i>The man who assumes everything is a lie is at least as mistaken as the one who assumes everything is true. If no guarantee can suit you, perhaps the flaw is not in the guarantee, but in you."</i> and <i>"well, people do get hypnotized by the hard choices. And stop looking for alternatives."</i> Bujold, I love those comments. they may not be the most mind-blowing things to read, but they do pop out at a person who is basically reading a bit of light, escapist space opera. that last quote in particular struck me, I deal with that on the council a lot, people I would otherwise respect talking about "making hard choices" when what they mean is that change is coming and we better start looking at which services we should slash or eliminate, as if that is actually hard when the actual hard work would be in figuring out how not to do unnecessary crap like that. ugh! I hate bullshit. unfortunately Miles spends some time thinking that bullshit too but there's a few other people around to set him straight. I have a fairly strong crush on Miles but I think that crush has expanded to the loyal and lovely Eli and her post-facial reconstruction take on the nature of beauty and of course walking boner Ivan and his amiable bickering. great supporting characters. and they live in a thoroughly enjoyable novel. this one has Miles traveling to Old Earth and getting caught up in various terrorist plots, oh Miles, you are always getting into trouble but fortunately you are a genius and so you always get yourself out of it. maybe a bit too easily at times, which is probably why this is 3 stars and not 4. and at long last, Miles' two identities and his schizophrenic lifestyle are fully explored and made central to the narrative. we have him splitting himself into two via a surprising tall tale that - <b>spoilers beyond this point</b> - turns out to be true, we have various characters finally addressing all of the issues that Miles faces in his two personas, and we have a great little hallucinogenic scene when he confusingly glimpses a very stressed-out version of himself across the way. best of all, we have a clone. yay for clones!<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/user/markmonday/media/mind2mindgif_zpscb5fcefe.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386829470ra/7453018.gif" alt=" photo mind2mindgif_zpscb5fcefe.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Miles and his clone don't really see eye to eye that way, and certainly not mind to mind. I guess I just love that gif. well, obviously, since it is the second time you've used it mark. for chrissakes find some new gifs already.<br><br>okay, Miles-style stream of consciousness review DONE.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16878046932195675568">As per usual, Miles Vorkosigan creates a stir wherever he goes. After figuratively hitting a wasp nest with a stick and annoying the Cetagandians, he hares off to old Earth to get his crew healthy and his ships fixed. Of course, things go horribly awry and lots of intrigue & adventure follows. <br/><br/>Somehow, for me, even though there are lots of action sequences, these books are more about the relationships. He has to balance his two identities as Lord Vorkosigan and Admiral Naismith, each with their </span>
  <span id="freeText16878046932195675568" style="display:none">As per usual, Miles Vorkosigan creates a stir wherever he goes. After figuratively hitting a wasp nest with a stick and annoying the Cetagandians, he hares off to old Earth to get his crew healthy and his ships fixed. Of course, things go horribly awry and lots of intrigue &amp; adventure follows. <br /><br />Somehow, for me, even though there are lots of action sequences, these books are more about the relationships. He has to balance his two identities as Lord Vorkosigan and Admiral Naismith, each with their own responsibilities. He has his cousin Ivan to consider, as Ivan is also stationed on Earth. Plus Miles makes friendships &amp; alliances wherever he goes—and they complicate an already intricate life. Finally there’s the question of whether he will ever get a personal life and find someone to love him as Miles, regardless of which identity he’s currently living in.<br /><br />Plenty of adventure here for those who like such things, and lots of character development for me. Another successful installment in the saga of Miles Vorkosigan.<br /><br />Book 261 in my Science Fiction and Fantasy Reading Project.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oleksandr Zholud" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oleksandr Zholud" href="/user/show/4743119-oleksandr-zholud">Oleksandr Zholud</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780786171088" href="/book/show/672979.Brothers_in_Arms">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3395041851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16818904754310315063">This is a SF space opera novel, part of Vorkosigan Saga, this time set almost completely on Earth (London to be precise). I’ve read it as a part of Vorkosigan Challenge at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hugo & Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br/><br/>This time Miles Vorkosigan in his guise as Admiral Naismith visits Earth chiefly to make some repairs of his Dendarii fleet after a successful, but costly in human life, operation of escaping from a military prison. Almost immediately he is interceded by a local reporter, who noted an un</span>
  <span id="freeText16818904754310315063" style="display:none">This is a SF space opera novel, part of Vorkosigan Saga, this time set almost completely on Earth (London to be precise). I’ve read it as a part of Vorkosigan Challenge at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo &amp; Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br /><br />This time Miles Vorkosigan in his guise as Admiral Naismith visits Earth chiefly to make some repairs of his Dendarii fleet after a successful, but costly in human life, operation of escaping from a military prison. Almost immediately he is interceded by a local reporter, who noted an uncanny resemblance between Barrayaran noble and mercenary leader. To put her off the truth, he on a spot (the way he have done before) concocts a story about Cetagandans creating his clone for some secret operation. The story however, soon bites him right back!<br /><br />It is not too sly tongue-in-a-cheek mocking of soap opera and space series tropes that a reader may ask themselves, is the author making fun of the genre or of me? I guess the former is the case and the genre in need of a bit of mockery. Moreover, as the story progresses, there are some interesting twists and more importantly, thought!<br /><br />A great installment in the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16818904754310315063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_492472392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492472392" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492472392?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=barrayar">barrayar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492472392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14762486530827808141"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>.</b><br/><br/>If I have to be completely honest this should have a 3 star rating. However I gave it a bonus star because it introduces one of my favourite support characters in the series - Duv Galeni. <br/><br/>Following the events of Dagoola and another operation soon after it the Dendarii are in a desperate need of some down time and to repair the damaged equipment. As a result they end up on Earth - the cradle of human civilization. And because this is Miles a simple repair job and </span>
  <span id="freeText14762486530827808141" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>.</b><br /><br />If I have to be completely honest this should have a 3 star rating. However I gave it a bonus star because it introduces one of my favourite support characters in the series - Duv Galeni. <br /><br />Following the events of Dagoola and another operation soon after it the Dendarii are in a desperate need of some down time and to repair the damaged equipment. As a result they end up on Earth - the cradle of human civilization. And because this is Miles a simple repair job and retrieval of the needed funds turns into a nightmare. Miles is a magnet for disasters :D Only he can stumble on a plot to destabilise the Barrayaran Empire totally by accident. Because he wasn't even supposed to go to Earth! I feel bad for all of Miles superiors. I think that they start weeping the moment they see that they are supposed to deal with him. Though for a change Miles doesn't kill the career of Capt. Galeni. They even form a strange friendship after all the things they go through together.<br /><br />Another major secondary character (I know it's kind of an oxymoron) is introduced - Mark, Miles' clone brother. He plays a major role in one of the following novels and is the catalyst for one of the biggest changes in Miles' life. Even saying so much is a spoiler for the rest of the series but I just couldn't explain why this is an important moment without mentioning it. Most of the time Miles reminds me of his father. Maybe it's because of the military situations he is in. However in regards to Mark, he shows how much Cordelia has been an influence on him. It takes a special kind of courage to do what he did. Courage or total lack of sense of self-preservation :D<br /><br />Ivan Vorpartil shows up and as usual gets drafted in. Miles is really hard on his friends and relatives. I do wonder why they haven't had him committed years ago just to avoid being collateral damage because of one of his plans ;) Again Ivan shows his remarkable ability to fool everyone into thinking him a harmless idiot so he can live his life the way he likes it. Unfortunately for him, Miles knows very well that he possesses a sharp mind and more importantly that he is loyal to a fault to his family. I can't wait to get to the book where Ivan is the main character. It's so much fun!<br /><br />Elli Quinn plays a bigger role and there's finally development on the romantic front. Miles is adorable when it comes to women - no dating or courtship, he goes straight for the jugular with the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[big question <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Miles, dear, thank the stars that Elli already loved you or you would have scared her away! <br /><br />There were some pretty intense scenes in this book and I remember how nerve wrecking it was to read them the first time. Now I could mostly laugh and enjoy the story without too much excess emotions. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14762486530827808141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2398854804" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10690054154403580080">At this point in the Vorkosigan chronology Miles has been living his double life as Admiral Naismith for several years and his Dendarii mercenaries are a thriving concern. The action picks up with the Dendarii arriving at Earth and Miles having to make his double identity work in ways that he hasn't in the past. There are people trying to kill him, and it may not just be his usual crowd of enemies, and nor is it clear who they're trying to kill: Vorkosigan or Naismith.<br/><br/>This is a fairly run-of-the</span>
  <span id="freeText10690054154403580080" style="display:none">At this point in the Vorkosigan chronology Miles has been living his double life as Admiral Naismith for several years and his Dendarii mercenaries are a thriving concern. The action picks up with the Dendarii arriving at Earth and Miles having to make his double identity work in ways that he hasn't in the past. There are people trying to kill him, and it may not just be his usual crowd of enemies, and nor is it clear who they're trying to kill: Vorkosigan or Naismith.<br /><br />This is a fairly run-of-the-mill off-Barrayar Vorkosigan story that would be familiar to anyone whose read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game__Vorkosigan_Saga___6_" title="The Vor Game (Vorkosigan Saga, #6) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vor Game</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76812.Cetaganda__Vorkosigan_Saga___9_" title="Cetaganda (Vorkosigan Saga, #9) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Cetaganda</a>. It does introduce some very important characters and relationships for later in the series though, particularly including Mark and Duv Galeni as well as establishing Elli Quinn a bit better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10690054154403580080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer660805037" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18349227735506740858"><b>**edit 11/26/13</b><br/><br/>My advice regarding the Vorkosigan Saga boils down to this: <b>
  <i>go read them. All of them.</i>
</b> I suggest starting with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_' title='The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warrior's Apprentice</a>--and no, this isn't one of my usual careless suggestions to jump midway into a series; it's recommended by Bujold herself. And now, onwards to <i>Brothers in Arms!</i><br/><br/>In Miles Vorkosigan's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296198.Borders_of_Infinity' rel='nofollow noopener'>most recent mission</a> as his alter-ego Admiral Miles Naismith of the Dendarii Free Mercenaries, he was sent undercover to rescue one important man from a Cetagandan </span>
  <span id="freeText18349227735506740858" style="display:none"><b>**edit 11/26/13</b><br /><br />My advice regarding the Vorkosigan Saga boils down to this: <b>
  <i>go read them. All of them.</i>
</b> I suggest starting with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a>--and no, this isn't one of my usual careless suggestions to jump midway into a series; it's recommended by Bujold herself. And now, onwards to <i>Brothers in Arms!</i><br /><br />In Miles Vorkosigan's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296198.Borders_of_Infinity" rel="nofollow noopener">most recent mission</a> as his alter-ego Admiral Miles Naismith of the Dendarii Free Mercenaries, he was sent undercover to rescue one important man from a Cetagandan POW camp. As is typical of Miles' missions, things didn't go as planned, and the 1 prisoner rescue was somehow multiplied into 10,000. Now, with the fleet badly in need of repairs, Miles has stopped at Old Earth to prize payment from the reluctant pockets of the Barrayaran Embassy in London. And, of course, that's when things on Earth start getting, as Miles would say, a little out of hand. While Miles is trying to escort high-faluting London socialites as part of his Barrayaran identity, he is forced to make a daring--and unfortunately visible--rescue as Admiral Naismith. With both of his identities seen on Earth, how long can it be before people connect the glaring fluorescent dots? As Miles points out, <i>"How many four-foot-nine-inch black-haired grey-eyed hunchbacks can there be on this damn planet? D’you think you trip over twitchy dwarfs on every street corner?"</i> Not only is his cover identity at risk, but, with the Cetagandans simultaneously meeting socially with with Lt. Vorkosigan of the Barrayaran Embassy and actively out for the blood of the all-too-similar Admiral Naismith, Miles is doubly in danger. Clearly, Miles decides, the obvious solution is to tell everyone that he has a clone, created in secret as part of a plot against Barrayar. It isn't long before Miles is heading straight into his own unique version of an identity crisis. And since this is Miles Vorkosigan, that's when things start getting complicated. <br />...<br />Due to <a href="http://pagefault.booklikes.com/post/713112/gr-debacle-101" rel="nofollow noopener">my disapproval</a> of GR's new and rather subjective review deletion policy, <a href="http://pagefault.booklikes.com/post/713964/-how-many-four-foot-nine-inch-black-haired-grey-eyed-hunchbacks-can-there-be-on-this-damn-planet-" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>the rest of my (typically verbose) review is posted over at Booklikes.</b>
</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_2330317133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330317133" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330317133?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=satirical-humorous">satirical-humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=humanistic-sf">humanistic-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=military-sf">military-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330317133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3684145106513251785"><b>Brothers in Arms: Miles gets seriously schizophrenic...or is it Admiral Naismith?</b><br/><br/>Now that I've thoroughly immersed in the <b>Miles Vorkosigan Saga</b>, like other fans I can begin to appreciate all the little character details that Bujold has carefully woven into each of the volumes, and as each of the seemingly small events of previous stories have larger repercussions later on, and previously minor characters take on greater importance and depth. This story takes places directly in the aftermath of t</span>
  <span id="freeText3684145106513251785" style="display:none"><b>Brothers in Arms: Miles gets seriously schizophrenic...or is it Admiral Naismith?</b><br /><br />Now that I've thoroughly immersed in the <b>Miles Vorkosigan Saga</b>, like other fans I can begin to appreciate all the little character details that Bujold has carefully woven into each of the volumes, and as each of the seemingly small events of previous stories have larger repercussions later on, and previously minor characters take on greater importance and depth. This story takes places directly in the aftermath of the prison camp breakout told in "Borders of Infinity" and explains why the Cetagandans are so upset with Miles.<br /><br />In <b>Brothers in Arms</b>, the Dendarii Mercenaries flee to Earth for much-needed repairs and recuperation after their latest misadventures. Miles contacts the local Barrayaran Embassy in London to get payment for his fleets expenses and repairs, but soon finds out the Cetagandans are on the hunt for a certain Admiral Naismith, who caused so much trouble to them recently. Never having had both Miles Vorkosigan and Admiral Naismith in the same place at the same time has avoided identity complications until this point, but now Miles must play both roles while avoiding Cetagandan assassins, his own Dendarii mercenaries causing trouble Earthside when their credit is found to be no good, and eventually a very sinister plot to undermine both Miles and Naismith long in the planning. The mastermind of this is just as clever as Miles is, and has a serious axe to grind with Miles. Also, his method of getting revenge introduces an intriguing and very conflicted new character to the story, who will take on even greater importance in the next volume <b>Mirror Dance</b>. <br /><br />This was a very enjoyable entry in the series, especially the difficulties that Miles encounters with his split identity, funding troubles for his fleet, more romantic entanglements, and finally some very intense drama as he encounters his nemesis in a tense finale in the city. Once again Bujold manages to seamlessly combine humor, improbable but madcap plot twists, tense action, but above all characters that you come to care about very much. All rolled into a fun-filled SF romp, but intelligent and above all humane.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3684145106513251785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_570519918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570519918" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570519918?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570519918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10110242129663426304">The series is definitely gaining momentum by this novel, changing tracks only a little from the previous stories. It introduces a short and surly wrinkle that will grow into one interesting character in his own right. This novel is more than an introduction for him, though. It's funny, clever, and does a deft job at worldbuilding Earth with barely touching it. Miles, like the reader (me), wanted to sightsee, but he was kept so busy we missed almost everything! And it should have been a vacation!</span>
  <span id="freeText10110242129663426304" style="display:none">The series is definitely gaining momentum by this novel, changing tracks only a little from the previous stories. It introduces a short and surly wrinkle that will grow into one interesting character in his own right. This novel is more than an introduction for him, though. It's funny, clever, and does a deft job at worldbuilding Earth with barely touching it. Miles, like the reader (me), wanted to sightsee, but he was kept so busy we missed almost everything! And it should have been a vacation!<br /><br />This was one of my easiest remembered rereads. It didn't spoil the enjoyment one iota to know what was coming. Such a great series!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5835136191177747369">Another fun adventure with Miles. This one is set in London, on Earth, which is a bit of a backwater. Other than that, it was pretty typically Miles - kind of crazy, a bit spastic, irreverent, & definitely twisty. As usual, none of Miles' superiors are very happy with him as he undermines & usurps their authority through sheer intelligence, energy, & force of personality. How he does this is most of the fun.<br/><br/>There wasn't anything really new & improved in this novel though, so I can only give it 3</span>
  <span id="freeText5835136191177747369" style="display:none">Another fun adventure with Miles. This one is set in London, on Earth, which is a bit of a backwater. Other than that, it was pretty typically Miles - kind of crazy, a bit spastic, irreverent, &amp; definitely twisty. As usual, none of Miles' superiors are very happy with him as he undermines &amp; usurps their authority through sheer intelligence, energy, &amp; force of personality. How he does this is most of the fun.<br /><br />There wasn't anything really new &amp; improved in this novel though, so I can only give it 3 stars. It's probably time to take a break from the series for a bit.</span>

  <span id="freeText122507157184600964" style="display:none">This series just keeps on getting better!<br /><br />For those who are unaware of this series: Miles Vorkosigan is a short officer who usually is looked down upon because of his appearance, but what people don't know is that he also accidentally became a mercenary captain and goes along with his fleet to war torn planets to save the day. He is hilarious and his quest in life is to be appreciated for the brilliant mind that he knows he is. <br />That is a very simplified plot to get you on the series. If you want to start from the beginning I recommend: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a> <br /><br />The series as any great sci-fi book has great technology and there are a lot of space traveling involve.<br /><br />If this doesn't make you want to start the series right away I don't know what will. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610767581" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/610767581?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6599568-brothers-in-arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=vorkosigan">vorkosigan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610767581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9055908001268568276">Miles and his Dendarri Mercenaries -- including his latest crush, Elli Quinn -- vist Earth for some R&R and basic shuttle repairs, but nothing is ever simple when Lord Miles Vorkosigan (Admiral Naismith) is around. From here, things grow even more complicated, because now there is a third Miles. His clone. Good thing cousin Ivan is around to cover his back.<br/><br/> I like this cover best:<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380420903i/835524._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='600' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>The Vorkosigan Saga</i> is space opera -- an adventurous lark across the cosmos, laced with danger, romance and philosop</span>
  <span id="freeText9055908001268568276" style="display:none">Miles and his Dendarri Mercenaries -- including his latest crush, Elli Quinn -- vist Earth for some R&amp;R and basic shuttle repairs, but nothing is ever simple when Lord Miles Vorkosigan (Admiral Naismith) is around. From here, things grow even more complicated, because now there is a third Miles. His clone. Good thing cousin Ivan is around to cover his back.<br><br> I like this cover best:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380420903i/835524._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Vorkosigan Saga</i> is space opera -- an adventurous lark across the cosmos, laced with danger, romance and philosophy. As science fiction, the "science" is not technical (fine by me). I read this series for the characterization and relationship development as well as the plot and pacing. The dialogue flows. In addition, Bujold occasionally inserts a word I hadn't heard before (I like that).<br><br>However, <b>
  <i>Brothers in Arms </i>
</b> did not appeal to me as well as some others. After reading her tightly paced novellas (~100 pages each) in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610006902" rel="nofollow noopener"> Borders of Infinity</a> this one seemed to bog down whenever Bujold retold events from prior books or described the historic conflict between planets Komarr and Barrayar.<br><br>Glad I stuck with it! Great confrontation scenes at the end, in the Tidewater Towers in London. I also enjoyed watching the relationship deepen between Miles and his cousin Ivan. Nice job with the characterization of Captain Duv Galeni. Hope to see more of him.<br><br>But there is a little <i>deus ex machina</i> going on. Several times, just as Miles stared death straight in the face...he's rescued. I like it better when he thinks his way out of his difficulties. Mind you, Miles did engage in strategic and philosophical analysis in this book, so I was mostly satisfied.<br><br>As this story opens, Miles is reflecting on the losses at the Dagoola IV POW camp (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609667160" rel="nofollow noopener">Borders of Infinity</a>). Since that amazing escape, the Cetagandans have been vengefully gunning for "Admiral Naismith" (Miles) and his mercenaries. Elli Quinn notes his tension:<blockquote>"I don't think I've ever seen a human being who needed to get laid worse than you do now." <br><br>(Commander Quinn seems willing, but there's that "no fraternizing" rule.) </blockquote>As one who enjoys a good romance, I was somewhat entertained by Miles and Elli -- and the living fur blanket they purchased. Elli's attachment to Miles felt real, especially given the events in <i>The Warrior's Apprentice</i> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608314215" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a>). However, I am not as certain about <i>his</i> attachment to her. Methinks he is not over Alena yet.<br><br><i>Brothers in Arms </i> is aptly named, in that Miles learns he has a clone. Miles, reflecting his progressive Betan upbringing with his admirable mother Cordelia (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595497342" rel="nofollow noopener">Shards of Honour</a>) immediately acknowledges his clone as his brother, and tells him he has a family and a name: Lord Mark Pierre Vorkosigan. But there are complications, not the least of which is that Mark has been raised since "birth" with one purpose -- to mimic Miles, kill Miles, replace Miles. This new "brotherhood" is not readily resolved and continues in <i>Mirror Dance.</i><br><br><b>More on Miles:</b> Simply put, Miles Vorkosigan is a brilliant mind in a brittle body. He's nothing to look at, standing not five-feet tall in his boots, with a skewed spine and bones that easily break (he's getting them replaced with super-strong plastic). I love to see him outsmart and out-bluff the big baddies. I chuckle at his fascination with tall, strong-willed women, especially redheads. He's a soft-hearted hero with a temper, an impulsive tyrant with boundless energy and ideas. His values are sound, his friendships true, and his escapades alternatively fascinating, worrisome, and hilarious.<br> <br>As a Barrayaran "Vor" (the military / warrior caste), Admiral of the Dendarii Mercenaries, and a secret agent working for ImpSec (Barrayaran Imperial Security), Miles is constantly in danger. In nearly every book, he gets busted up and/or loses a friend or comrade. Bujold does death fairly well -- the grief, the loss, the guilt and sorrow.<br><br>Age: In this book, Miles is a lieutenant, age 27, by my calculations, or else 25 (the sequel Mirror Dance also puts him at about 27, yet it's set two years after, so that would be a disconnect. A few minor inconsistencies do crop up across the series, maybe because the books were not published in chronological order. Perhaps I miscalculated).<br><br>======<br><br><b>Planet Barrayar and the Vor Lords:</b> Many names sound the same. On planet Barrayar -- where Miles was born -- noble houses begin with Vor, as with Miles Vorkosigan, emperor Gregor Vorbarra, Ivan Vorpatril, etc. "Vor-" is a prefix that means "military warrior" or something similar. This naming system began about 600 years ago, after Barrayar's wormhole to Mother Earth collapsed and the Period of Isolation began, transforming (and regressing) advanced Barrayar into a feudal system of government. Barrayarans are descendants of Russian, English, French, and Greek colonists. <br><br>=======<br><br> <b> My reviews of this series (*favorites): </b> <br><br>Shards of Honor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595497342" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*Barrayar <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600881270" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*The Warrior's Apprentice <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608314215" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>The Vor Game <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621247875" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Cetaganda <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621248447" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>The Mountains of Mourning <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608861209" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Labyrinth <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609404500" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*Borders of Infinity <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609667160" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Brothers in Arms <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610767581" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Mirror Dance <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/612039450" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*Memory <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/616335905" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*Miles in Love: Komarr, A Civil Campaign, Winterfair Gifts <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615383102" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>*Komarr <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614469322" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Diplomatic Immunity <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/617452384" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Captain Vorpatril's Alliance <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623244088" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a><br>Cryoburn <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618074515" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9055908001268568276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1078169009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078169009" />
    <a title="Rosario (http://rosario.blogspot.com/)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13656797-rosario-http-rosario-blogspot-com"><img alt="Rosario (http://rosario.blogspot.com/)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350319469p2/13656797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078169009?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosario (http://rosario.blogspot.com/)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosario (http://rosario.blogspot.com/)" href="/user/show/13656797-rosario-http-rosario-blogspot-com">Rosario (http://rosario.blogspot.com/)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078169009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15478893077057224137">Right, let's catch up with the Vorkosigan books. I'm up to Memory now and probably won't be able to hold on much longer before reading even further, so best post a couple of reviews before they all become muddled in my mind.<br/><br/>It's not long after the rescue mission told in the wonderful Borders of Infinity, and Miles and the Dendarii mercenaries decide to make a pit stop on good old Earth. There are some necessary repairs to be made, plus, Miles thinks it's a good idea to be somewhere he can keep a</span>
  <span id="freeText15478893077057224137" style="display:none">Right, let's catch up with the Vorkosigan books. I'm up to Memory now and probably won't be able to hold on much longer before reading even further, so best post a couple of reviews before they all become muddled in my mind.<br /><br />It's not long after the rescue mission told in the wonderful Borders of Infinity, and Miles and the Dendarii mercenaries decide to make a pit stop on good old Earth. There are some necessary repairs to be made, plus, Miles thinks it's a good idea to be somewhere he can keep away from the Cetagandans. <br /><br />Turning back into Lord Vorkosigan, Miles reports to the Barrayarran embassy. He just needs money from ImpSec for repairs and to pay his people, but the highest-ranking ImpSec officer, who happens to be a Komarran, isn't particularly impressed with him. The payroll, which Miles expected would be there soonish, is taking much longer than it should, and Miles suspects shenanigans. <br /><br />And, this being Miles, he's constitutionally unable to just wait quietly. Before long he's managed to get into the public eye and is having to come up with a story to explain just why Admiral Naismith looks so similar to Lord Vorkosigan.<br /><br />This was great. It's a bit of a farce, with people (not quite literally, but almost!) going out one door and in through another, mistaken identities and ridiculous plots and mad chases. And this starts a run of books that deal with the issue of identity in a way that I found fresh and very thought-provoking. The schizophrenic nature of Miles' dual identity comes to the forefront here, and the most implausible tall tales come true in a delicious way. I don't want to give away anything, but this starts a relationship that I've loved in the following books, and that succeeded here in being really intriguing and having great potential. And in addition to identity (or rather, as an extension to identity), Brothers in Arms has some interesting things to say about fathers and sons and how the former can shape the latter. This is when this light romp becomes something a bit weightier, and it works.<br /><br />What else? Oh, we get some great scenes. There's Miles out-bullshitting a journalist, Miles on Fast-Penta, Ivan bamboozled, and we also find out some more about the complicated history between Barrayar and Komarr, last seen by readers in Aral and Cordelia's books. We now see more about what's been going on since, with Komarr being part of the Barrayarran Empire but many people there still considering Aral The Butcher of Komarr. Again, more on this in later books, and this lays the base very nicely. Oh, and we're introduced to Miles' Komarran commanding officer, Captain Duv Galeni, who is a particularly good character here and only becomes even better later.<br /><br />We also get a nice romance between Miles and Elli Quinn here. Miles had previously succeeded in staying away from her (non-fraternisation rules seemed like a good idea when he came up with them), in spite of her obvious interest, but things change here. I like Elli Quinn very much and obviously, I love Miles, but the two of them as a couple don't really do a huge deal for me. I mean, they are clearly fond of each other, but it's just as clear that this isn't a huge, life-long love, no matter how much Miles tries to tell himself otherwise. <br /><br />I highly recommend this one. Just one thing: be very cautious when reading descriptions of the Vorkosigan books, especially this one and the ones after. Too many people who love these books seem to think that no one's reading the series for the first time, so spoilers are just fine. And big spoilers, too. Even the blurbs are sometimes an issue.There's a big thing we find out here that I would have loved to have been a surprise, but no such luck (someone posted a review of an earlier book that said "of course, Miles' so-and-so hasn't yet shown up here". Cheers for that!). It didn't ruin the reading experience, or anything, but it would have been nice not to know!<br /><br />MY GRADE: A very strong B+. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15478893077057224137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_9267572" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9267572" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/627337-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261273615p2/627337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9267572?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/627337-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=z2019-reads">z2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=sff-science-fiction">sff-science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9267572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11011955810831925810">**** 2019 re-read ***<br/><br/>This book is that start of what I feel is a stellar, could-almost-stand-alone trilogy within the series. This book and the next two, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance__Vorkosigan_Saga___8_' title='Mirror Dance (Vorkosigan Saga, #8) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mirror Dance</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_' title='Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Memory</a> introduce Mark and through him sets off a series of events that culminate in what I feel is an ending of sorts and marks and turning point and new beginning for Miles.<br/><br/>I once likened this book to a Shakespearan comedy of errors, because it really feels like one, albeit in space. Miles is left cooling his heels on earth an</span>
  <span id="freeText11011955810831925810" style="display:none">**** 2019 re-read ***<br /><br />This book is that start of what I feel is a stellar, could-almost-stand-alone trilogy within the series. This book and the next two, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance__Vorkosigan_Saga___8_" title="Mirror Dance (Vorkosigan Saga, #8) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_" title="Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Memory</a> introduce Mark and through him sets off a series of events that culminate in what I feel is an ending of sorts and marks and turning point and new beginning for Miles.<br /><br />I once likened this book to a Shakespearan comedy of errors, because it really feels like one, albeit in space. Miles is left cooling his heels on earth and as his space-faring past begins to catch up with him and needing to preserve his real identity cover, through some very Miles Machinations, he spins an outlandish story out of whole cloth. Which actually turns out to be true much to the horrified surprise of our hero. During that we get treated to a little more history of Barrayar and Komarr, fake identity shenanigans, people masquerading as other people. And an usual a twisty plot and elegant solution to a thorny problem. Also great dashes of humor.<br /><br />And as I noted in my previous review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76812.Cetaganda__Vorkosigan_Saga___9_" title="Cetaganda (Vorkosigan Saga, #9) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Cetaganda</a> we get introduced to a new character who, through being pulled into Miles' execrable orbit, comes out the better personally and professionally for it.<br /><br /><br /><br />**********************Previous review***************************<br /><br />Taken as a whole, the Miles Vorkosigan series is simply outstanding. The series is built around the character of Miles. And through them we learn about his world, the forces that created him, how he thinks and acts and the people who love, hate, respect and revere him.<br /><br />Taken as parts of the a whole, the books each stand on their own merits and, although are ostensibly classified as Science Fiction, I find that they could be cross-classified with other genres.<br /><br /><i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a>
</i> and <i>The Vor Game</i>, imo are unabashed rollicking space opera.<br /><br /><i>Brothers at Arms</i> feels like a Shakespearean comedy of errors.<br /><br /><i>Mirror Dance</i> and <i>Borders of Infinity</i> would not be out of place along side of those taut Robert Ludlum thrillers.<br /><br /><i>Memory</i> and <i>Komarr</i> are mystery novels. With <i> Memory</i> being a nice whodunnit while <i>Komarr</i> is closer to being a police procedural.<br /><br />And <i>A Civil Campaign</i> is a sparkling delight of a romance novel, reminiscent of something Georgette Heyer would write.<br /><br />As different as each book feels thematically, they all work together to complete a great character study of one of my very favorite fictional characters.<br /><br />I truly envy those who have not yet read these books. As I find new authors and new books to read, I can only hope to once again experience the feeling of discovering something truly great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11011955810831925810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3312049357" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3312049357" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3312049357?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29216335-brothers-in-arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=american-authors">american-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=set-in-space">set-in-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3312049357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3997025175299888814">This installment of the Vorkosigan Saga follows directly on from the novella, Borders of Infinity. In Borders Miles had battled and outwitted the Cetagandans, resulting in a price put on his head and the Dendarii fleet in need of some time to recover economically and emotionally. They choose to do so on Earth; in particular London. <br/><br/>It soon turns out to be no relaxing and rejuvenating break. Miles has to deal with Fleet money issues, a new superior at the Barrayaran embassy, and his evolving feel</span>
  <span id="freeText3997025175299888814" style="display:none">This installment of the Vorkosigan Saga follows directly on from the novella, Borders of Infinity. In Borders Miles had battled and outwitted the Cetagandans, resulting in a price put on his head and the Dendarii fleet in need of some time to recover economically and emotionally. They choose to do so on Earth; in particular London. <br /><br />It soon turns out to be no relaxing and rejuvenating break. Miles has to deal with Fleet money issues, a new superior at the Barrayaran embassy, and his evolving feelings for Elli, who has had a sweet crush on him since The Warrior's Apprentice. Miles's biggest dilemma though is juggling his double life of Admiral Naismith of the Dendarii Fleet and Lord Vorkosigan, son of the Barrayar Prime Minister. In a tough spot with a reporters and the police, Miles invents a story in a vain attempt to prove his two identities are separate persons - he claims he was cloned. In a twist that unfortunately we all see coming (see below) Miles discovers that this story he’d invented on the spur of the moment could actually be true.<br /><br />Overall, plot wise, this is probably my favourite Miles adventure yet but it was spoiled by a couple of things - the first being spoilers.<br /><br />Yes, the detail of the clone storyline is basically impossible to avoid. Nearly every review mentions it, discussions on the series mention it, it's even advertised on the book covers (as usual, nearly all the covers are horrendous). If this isn't enough, the next book in the series mentions some of the details on the blurb and shows us two Miles on the cover. So, with not even LMB or the publishers creating a spoiler free environment, the twist and big reveal was a bit anticlimactic. A shame too, considering it was quite a way into the book and so well done. <br /><br />My other complaint with the book is that Miles once again manages to get himself out of trouble so easily. Yes, LMB always creates conflict beautifully by throwing Miles in the proverbial deep end every chance she gets, but I often find he manages to extract himself and his friends from harm’s way with relative ease which, I admit, lessens the tension. Sometimes I wish things would drag on a little longer before Miles has to move on to his next crisis.<br /><br />I also realise LMB writes these books completely from Miles’s point of view but I did, at times, long for the point of view of the other characters (in particular, his cousin Ivan and Elli's) in this installment. <br /><br />LMB usually wins me over with Miles’s soul searching and poignant moments and she did this once again with some fine moments revolving around Miles’s relationship with his parents, Ivan, and Elli. *sniff* I also loved how Miles’s love for, and loyalty to, his family and home planet are depicted in this book. It's a recurring theme of Brothers In Arms and adds meaning to the title. <br /><br />Another highlight of the book was the inclusion of Captain Galeni, whose presence not only brings us up to date with what has happened to the Komarrans since Aral’s defeat of the planet, but also introduces us to a new supporting character whom I hope will pop up again in the series. <br /><br />After being in a bit of rut reading-wise lately, this book really excited me to continue with the series.<br /><br />4, heading towards 4 ½ out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="3997025175299888814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81074628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81074628" />
    <a title="Kathi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2179275-kathi"><img alt="Kathi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554852286p2/2179275.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81074628?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathi" href="/user/show/2179275-kathi">Kathi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2179275-kathi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer81074628&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81074628" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12636418183496860983">Miles Vorkosigan and his alter ego, Admiral Naismith, are closely intertwined in this story--sometimes it's as confusing for the reader as it is for Miles, but Bujold certainly handles it deftly. Then she adds to the confusion! It never occurred to me that Miles's comment to the reporter about there being a clone of him would turn out to be true, and a clone planned & paid for by Komarrans--never saw that coming!<br/><br/>Interesting tidbits that stood out for me: Miles's realization that giving Elli such</span>
  <span id="freeText12636418183496860983" style="display:none">Miles Vorkosigan and his alter ego, Admiral Naismith, are closely intertwined in this story--sometimes it's as confusing for the reader as it is for Miles, but Bujold certainly handles it deftly. Then she adds to the confusion! It never occurred to me that Miles's comment to the reporter about there being a clone of him would turn out to be true, and a clone planned &amp; paid for by Komarrans--never saw that coming!<br /><br />Interesting tidbits that stood out for me: Miles's realization that giving Elli such a beautiful face was not necessarily the gift he initially thought it was, but Elli is a stronger and more capable officer because of it. Miles's longing for Elena, so thoroughly buried but so heart-breakingly real, was very touching and deeply moving.<br /><br />As always, the center of each Miles tale seems to be about second chances, about overcoming one's circumstances, about making difficult choices and accepting the consequences, about learning who one really is and what is truly important, which may be different for each character.<br /><br />So, why 4 stars and not 5? A bit too many identity switches, and some over-stretching of the limits of believability, even for Bujold.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12636418183496860983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/12420909-brothers-in-arms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>,

          </div>
